# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Grafana Plugin Security Signature Verification

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in grafana/grafana that implement plugin signature verification: the plugin manifest signing, the signature validation on load, and the unsigned plugin allowlist enforcement.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the compliance domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec` (grafana/grafana)
- `sg-evals/grafana-loki` (grafana/loki)
- `sg-evals/grafana-mimir` (grafana/mimir)


82-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of Grafana's plugin signature verification system and created the answer file.

## Summary

I've identified and documented **17 Go source files** that implement plugin signature verification in grafana/grafana. The system has three main components:

### 1. **Plugin Manifest Signing** (pkg/plugins/manager/signature/)
- `manifest.go` - Core `Signature` struct with `Calculate()` method that reads MANIFEST.txt, validates PGP signatures, and verifies file hashes
- `statickey/static_retriever.go` - Hard-coded Grafana public key for manifest verification

### 2. **Signature Validation on Load** (pkg/plugins/manager/pipeline/)
- `signature/signature.go` - `Validation.ValidateSignature()` validates signatures during plugin initialization
- `validation/steps.go` - `SignatureValidationStep()` integrates signature validation into the plugin loader pipeline
- `bootstrap/steps.go` - `DefaultConstructor.Construct()` calculates signature status during bootstrap

### 3. **Unsigned Plugin Allowlist Enforcement** (pkg/plugins/manager/signature/)
- `authorizer.go` - `UnsignedPluginAuthorizer.CanLoadPlugin()` enforces the PluginsAllowUnsigned configuration
- `pkg/setting/setting_plugins.go` - Reads `allow_loading_unsigned_plugins` config

### Key Features:
- **Static Key Retrieval**: Built-in Grafana-signed key with ID `7e4d0c6a708866e7`
- **Dynamic Key Retrieval**: Downloads keys from Grafana.com API with 10-day cache
- **Signature States**: internal, valid, invalid, modified, unsigned
- **Signature Types**: grafana, commercial, community, private, private-glob
- **File Integrity**: SHA256 hash verification for all plugin files
- **Development Mode**: Allows unsigned plugins when DevMode is enabled

signature verification system is implemented across multiple components in the plugin manager and pluginsintegration packages. The system handles three main aspects: plugin manifest signing, signature validation on load, and unsigned plugin allowlist enforcement.\\n\\n## Plugin Manifest Signing\\n\\nThe core signature calculation happens in `pkg/plugins/manager/signature/manifest.go` through the `Signature` struct which implements the `SignatureCalculator` interface. The `Calculate()` method performs the following:\\n\\n1. **Manifest Reading**: `ReadPluginManifestFromFS()` opens and reads the `MANIFEST.txt` file from the plugin's filesystem. If not found, it returns `ErrSignatureTypeUnsigned`.\\n\\n2. **Manifest Parsing and Validation**: `readPluginManifest()` decodes the PGP-signed manifest using `clearsign.Decode()` and parses the JSON payload into a `PluginManifest` struct.\\n\\n3. **Manifest Validation**: `validateManifest()` ensures all required fields are present:\\n   - Basic fields: plugin, version, keyId, time, files\\n   - V2-specific fields: signedByOrg, signedByOrgName, signatureType\\n   - Calls `Verify()` to validate the PGP signature\\n\\n4. **Signature Verification**: `Verify()` retrieves the public key via `KeyRetriever.GetPublicKey()` and validates the PGP signature using `openpgp.CheckDetachedSignature()`.\\n\\n5. **File Hash Verification**: `verifyHash()` verifies each file's SHA256 hash matches the manifest's recorded hash. It detects modified plugins by comparing hashes of actual files against manifest entries.\\n\\n6. **Signature Status Determination**: The `Calculate()` method returns:\\n   - `SignatureStatusValid` for properly signed plugins with matching hashes\\n   - `SignatureStatusInvalid` for v1 manifests or invalid signatures\\n   - `SignatureStatusModified` for valid signatures with file hash mismatches\\n   - `SignatureStatusUnsigned` for plugins without MANIFEST.txt\\n\\n## Key Retrieval System\\n\\nPlugin manifest verification requires public keys. The system supports two modes:\\n\\n**Static Keys** (`pkg/plugins/manager/signature/statickey/static_retriever.go`): The default `KeyRetriever` contains a hard-coded Grafana-signed public key with ID `7e4d0c6a708866e7`. The `GetPublicKey()` method returns this key for Grafana-signed plugins.\\n\\n**Dynamic Keys** (`pkg/services/pluginsintegration/keyretriever/dynamic/dynamic_retriever.go`): When enabled via configuration, the `KeyRetriever` downloads public keys from the Grafana.com API endpoint `/plugins/ci/keys`. It caches keys in a key store with a 10-day sync interval. The `downloadKeys()` method retrieves and caches `ManifestKeys` records containing keyId and public key content. The `GetPublicKey()` method looks up keys from the cache, falling back to the default key if not found.\\n\\nThe `pkg/services/pluginsintegration/keyretriever/retriever.go` `Service` acts as a selector, delegating to dynamic keys if enabled, otherwise using static keys.\\n\\n## Signature Validation on Load\\n\\nDuring the plugin loading pipeline, signature validation occurs in two stages:\\n\\n**Bootstrap Stage** (`pkg/plugins/manager/pipeline/bootstrap/steps.go`): The `DefaultConstructor.Construct()` method calls `signatureCalculator.Calculate()` to compute the signature status for each plugin. This populates the plugin's `Signature`, `SignatureType`, and `SignatureOrg` fields.\\n\\n**Validation Stage** (`pkg/plugins/manager/signature/signature.go` and `pkg/plugins/manager/pipeline/validation/steps.go`): The `Validation.ValidateSignature()` method is called for each bootstrapped plugin. It:\\n\\n1. Returns nil (success) if signature is valid or plugin is core\\n2. For unsigned plugins: calls `UnsignedPluginAuthorizer.CanLoadPlugin()` to check the allowlist\\n3. Returns error for invalid or modified signatures\\n4. Handles inherited signatures for nested child plugins\\n\\nThe validation pipeline is orchestrated in `pkg/plugins/manager/pipeline/validation/validation.go` through the `Validate()` method, which runs all configured validation steps including `SignatureValidationStep()`.\\n\\n## Unsigned Plugin Allowlist Enforcement\\n\\nThe unsigned plugin allowlist is implemented in `pkg/plugins/manager/signature/authorizer.go` through the `UnsignedPluginAuthorizer` struct. The `CanLoadPlugin()` method enforces the allowlist by:\\n\\n1. Allowing all plugins if signature status is not unsigned (already signed/valid)\\n2. Allowing all unsigned plugins in development mode (when `DevMode` is true)\\n3. Checking the `PluginsAllowUnsigned` list from configuration: if the plugin ID matches an entry in this list, it returns true\\n4. Returning false (rejecting the plugin) otherwise\\n\\nThe configuration is read in `pkg/setting/setting_plugins.go` from the INI file key `allow_loading_unsigned_plugins` and stored in `pkg/setting/setting.go` as part of the `Cfg` struct's `PluginsAllowUnsigned` field. signature verification system is implemented across multiple components in the plugin manager and pluginsintegration packages. The system handles three main aspects: plugin manifest signing, signature validation on load, and unsigned plugin allowlist enforcement.\\n\\n## Plugin Manifest Signing\\n\\nThe core signature calculation happens in `pkg/plugins/manager/signature/manifest.go` through the `Signature` struct which implements the `SignatureCalculator` interface. The `Calculate()` method performs the following:\\n\\n1. **Manifest Reading**: `ReadPluginManifestFromFS()` opens and reads the `MANIFEST.txt` file from the plugin's filesystem. If not found, it returns `ErrSignatureTypeUnsigned`.\\n\\n2. **Manifest Parsing and Validation**: `readPluginManifest()` decodes the PGP-signed manifest using `clearsign.Decode()` and parses the JSON payload into a `PluginManifest` struct.\\n\\n3. **Manifest Validation**: `validateManifest()` ensures all required fields are present:\\n   - Basic fields: plugin, version, keyId, time, files\\n   - V2-specific fields: signedByOrg, signedByOrgName, signatureType\\n   - Calls `Verify()` to validate the PGP signature\\n\\n4. **Signature Verification**: `Verify()` retrieves the public key via `KeyRetriever.GetPublicKey()` and validates the PGP signature using `openpgp.CheckDetachedSignature()`.\\n\\n5. **File Hash Verification**: `verifyHash()` verifies each file's SHA256 hash matches the manifest's recorded hash. It detects modified plugins by comparing hashes of actual files against manifest entries.\\n\\n6. **Signature Status Determination**: The `Calculate()` method returns:\\n   - `SignatureStatusValid` for properly signed plugins with matching hashes\\n   - `SignatureStatusInvalid` for v1 manifests or invalid signatures\\n   - `SignatureStatusModified` for valid signatures with file hash mismatches\\n   - `SignatureStatusUnsigned` for plugins without MANIFEST.txt\\n\\n## Key Retrieval System\\n\\nPlugin manifest verification requires public keys. The system supports two modes:\\n\\n**Static Keys** (`pkg/plugins/manager/signature/statickey/static_retriever.go`): The default `KeyRetriever` contains a hard-coded Grafana-signed public key with ID `7e4d0c6a708866e7`. The `GetPublicKey()` method returns this key for Grafana-signed plugins.\\n\\n**Dynamic Keys** (`pkg/services/pluginsintegration/keyretriever/dynamic/dynamic_retriever.go`): When enabled via configuration, the `KeyRetriever` downloads public keys from the Grafana.com API endpoint `/plugins/ci/keys`. It caches keys in a key store with a 10-day sync interval. The `downloadKeys()` method retrieves and caches `ManifestKeys` records containing keyId and public key content. The `GetPublicKey()` method looks up keys from the cache, falling back to the default key if not found.\\n\\nThe `pkg/services/pluginsintegration/keyretriever/retriever.go` `Service` acts as a selector, delegating to dynamic keys if enabled, otherwise using static keys.\\n\\n## Signature Validation on Load\\n\\nDuring the plugin loading pipeline, signature validation occurs in two stages:\\n\\n**Bootstrap Stage** (`pkg/plugins/manager/pipeline/bootstrap/steps.go`): The `DefaultConstructor.Construct()` method calls `signatureCalculator.Calculate()` to compute the signature status for each plugin. This populates the plugin's `Signature`, `SignatureType`, and `SignatureOrg` fields.\\n\\n**Validation Stage** (`pkg/plugins/manager/signature/signature.go` and `pkg/plugins/manager/pipeline/validation/steps.go`): The `Validation.ValidateSignature()` method is called for each bootstrapped plugin. It:\\n\\n1. Returns nil (success) if signature is valid or plugin is core\\n2. For unsigned plugins: calls `UnsignedPluginAuthorizer.CanLoadPlugin()` to check the allowlist\\n3. Returns error for invalid or modified signatures\\n4. Handles inherited signatures for nested child plugins\\n\\nThe validation pipeline is orchestrated in `pkg/plugins/manager/pipeline/validation/validation.go` through the `Validate()` method, which runs all configured validation steps including `SignatureValidationStep()`.\\n\\n## Unsigned Plugin Allowlist Enforcement\\n\\nThe unsigned plugin allowlist is implemented in `pkg/plugins/manager/signature/authorizer.go` through the `UnsignedPluginAuthorizer` struct. The `CanLoadPlugin()` method enforces the allowlist by:\\n\\n1. Allowing all plugins if signature status is not unsigned (already signed/valid)\\n2. Allowing all unsigned plugins in development mode (when `DevMode` is true)\\n3. Checking the `PluginsAllowUnsigned` list from configuration: if the plugin ID matches an entry in this list, it returns true\\n4. Returning false (rejecting the plugin) otherwise\\n\\nThe configuration is read in `pkg/setting/setting_plugins.go` from the INI file key `allow_loading_unsigned_plugins` and stored in `pkg/setting/setting.go` as part of the `Cfg` struct's `PluginsAllowUnsigned` field. This configuration is passed to `pkg/plugins/config/config.go` through `PluginManagementCfg.PluginsAllowUnsigned`.\\n\\n## Plugin Loading Pipeline Integration\\n\\nThe complete signature verification chain is orchestrated in `pkg/plugins/manager/loader/loader.go`. The `Load()` method:\\n\\n1. Discovers plugins\\n2. Bootstraps them (calculating signatures)\\n3. Validates them (checking signatures and enforcing allowlists)\\n4. Initializes them\\n\\nThe `pkg/services/pluginsintegration/loader/loader.go` `Loader` wraps this implementation and provides the `Load()` interface for the broader plugin integration system.\\n\\n## Model Definitions\\n\\nSignature-related types are defined in `pkg/plugins/models.go`:\\n- `SignatureStatus`: internal, valid, invalid, modified, unsigned\\n- `SignatureType`: grafana, commercial, community, private, private-glob\\n- `Signature`: struct containing status, type, and signing organization\\n\\nThese types are used throughout the system to track and enforce plugin signature verification.\"\n}\n",
